This creates more access routes for our brains to get at the desired information, and thus increases ease of recall. Valley of the Queens located near the better known Valley of the Kings, on the west bank of the Nile river across from Thebes (Luxor).\r\n\r\nSenet is a board game from predynastic and ancient Egypt, it is the earliest known record of a backgammon , checkers, draughts, ludo and chess like games.\r\n\r\nThe oldest hieroglyph representing a Senet game dates to around 3500 BC.The full name of the game in Egyptian was meaning \"The game of passing\".\r\n\r\nGames have been around for thousands of years, but none are older than the ancient game of Senet, invented by the Egyptians roughly 3500 or 5000 years ago. It is believed that this two-player board game originated as a popular form of recreation with both royalty and peasantry. But by the mid-13th century BC, Senet had evolved into a more religious ritual. Some depictions from this time period forward show the game being played not by two people, but rather as a deceased player competing against an invisible adversary, interpreted by some to symbolize the deceased players own soul.\r\n\r\nThe board has become a metaphor for the afterlife with pawns moving across the board just as a soul moves through layers of the netherworld after death. Reaching the final space and leaving the board is the goal of the game, just as reaching Horus and leaving the netherworld was the goal for the Egyptians after their death for attaining rebirth with the gods Isis & Osiris, Sekhmet & Bastet holding the Egyptian Ankh or the papyrus scepter.\r\n\r\nThe game board consists of 30 squares or slots, arranged in 3 horizontal rows of 10. Pawns move from left to right through row 1, then drop down and move from right to left through row 2. Dropping down again, pawns move from left to right along row 3 and finally, off the board. The game uses the rules developed by Timothy Kendall in his 1978 work, Passing Through the Netherworld :The Meaning and Play of Senet, an Ancient Egyptian Funerary Game.\r\n\r\nThe game includes five special squares, governed by their own rules, each containing a hieroglyphic. Square 15 is the House of Rebirth; square 26 is the House of Beauty; square 27 is the House of Water: square 28 is the House of the Three Truths; square 29 is the House of Two Truths; and square 30, the last, is the House of Horus, the Egyptian falcon-god and lord of the sky.\r\n\r\nEgyptian Senet is a pharaonic challenging game that combines luck,strategy,and magic features authentic photos of ancient Egyptian temples,plus artistically crafted graphics and animation of an ancient stone game board and pieces,set in an echoing,tomb-like chamber.Ritualistic music plus sound effects of stone pieces moving recreate the atmosphere of predynastic Egypt.The App's Icon shows the Egyptian Queen Nefertari playing Senet in her tomb,she was the great wife of the pharaoh Ramesses II(Ramses)Rio. Después de que su hijo use Matemáticas amigables varias veces, la aplicación comenzará a elegir preguntas que desafían suavemente la capacidad de su hijo sin desalentar el progreso. Otras aplicaciones eran juegos cronometrados que ofrecían respuestas de opción múltiple. Mi preocupación con ésos era que los cabritos aprendieron presionar rápidamente los botones correctos sin mucha comprensión del tema.\r\n\r\nMatemáticas amigables se desarrolló para abordar algunas de estas preocupaciones. Con Matemáticas amigables, los niños no son cronometrados con el fin de permitirles tiempo para pensar, consolidar el conocimiento y entender verdaderamente los problemas. Las respuestas incorrectas no son penalizadas y la aplicación a menudo ofrece segundas oportunidades. Creo que este enfoque alienta el espíritu de aprendizaje y experimentación. El refuerzo positivo se utiliza, no la puntuación negativa. Esto evita que los niños formen actitudes negativas hacia las matemáticas y proteja su autoestima. El diseño visual simple de las aplicaciones ayuda a los niños a concentrarse en las matemáticas con un mínimo de distracciones, de modo que el aprendizaje puede transferirse fácilmente a las pruebas escolares y escenarios de la vida real.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigables proporciona a su hijo con recompensas en forma de logros coleccionables. Para obtener el mejor efecto, se anima a los padres a proporcionar refuerzo positivo adicional vinculando los logros de la aplicación con recompensas adicionales. Usted sabe mejor qué trabaja para su niño, si es dinero de bolsillo adicional, tiempo de la pantalla, llevándolos en un viaje o nada en absoluto. Cada logro se desbloquea contestando 100 preguntas correctamente, lo que se puede hacer en una sesión o dos. Idealmente, su hijo debe ser alentado a utilizar la aplicación un par de veces a la semana, por lo que 3 o 4 logros a la semana debe ser óptimo. Una vez más, se debe lograr un equilibrio aquí. Demasiado poco uso puede no proporcionar beneficios óptimos, pero demasiado uso puede resultar en actitudes negativas y fatiga. Una vez más, usted sabe mejor lo que es óptimo para su hijo.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigables pueden ser utilizadas por hasta cinco niños siempre y cuando estén compartiendo una computadora. Es importante que cada niño juegue bajo su \"login\" ya que la aplicación adapta las preguntas a su hijo. Si tienen dispositivos dedicados, necesitarán una licencia separada para cada niño.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigas le permite instalar la aplicación en varios dispositivos y el progreso seguirá a su hijo a medida que cambia los dispositivos. Por lo tanto, su hijo puede comenzar en un dispositivo y seguir jugando en otro.\r\n \r\nHe hecho todo lo posible para diseñar matemáticas amigables para requisitos especiales de accesibilidad, pero tengo recursos limitados para probar esto. The game is played with a standard deck of cards (including 2 jokers). \r\n\r\nPlayers are dealt a total of 12 cards.  The remaining 6 cards are dealt face down into the 'Kitty'.  Each player will bid starting clockwise from the dealer (dealer bids last).  \r\nThe bid consists of a bid number and description.  The bid number is the number of tricks (books) a player believes his partnership can achieve over 6. For example, a bid of 4 = 10 books. \r\n\r\nThe bid description indicates a bid direction (High or Low) or whether the bid is a 'No' trump. A bid direction of High (Uptown) indicates A,K,Q... are the highest value cards. A bid direction of Low (Downtown, Special) indicates A,2,3... are the highest value cards. A 'No' trump bid indicates that each suit has equal weight and the lead card can not be 'cut'.  The bid direction of a 'No' bid is specified after winning the bid.\r\nBid numbers can range from 3 - 7.  The Option screen gives the player the option of playing with a minimum of 3 or 4.\r\nBid descriptions have the following weights:  'No' > 'Low' > 'High'.  The Option screen allows the player to play make 'Low' and 'High' equal in weight: 'No' > 'Low' = 'High'. \r\n\r\nThe highest bidder indicates a 'trump' suit or in the case of a 'No' bid indicates the direction (High/Low).  The jokers become the highest value cards in the indicated 'trump' suit.  For example, if Diamonds were called as 'trump' the highest value cards for a 'High' direction would be:  Big Joker, Little Joker, A, K,...  In the case of a 'No' bid, the Big Joker and Little Joker have no value and should be discarded as soon as possible.\r\n\r\nThe bid winner will start play as the lead player.  The remaining players must play a card in the same suit as the lead card if available. If the player does not have a card in that suit they may play another suit. The highest value card in the lead suit wins the sequence unless a trump card is played in which case the highest trump card wins the sequence. The winner of the sequence will be the lead player in the following sequence. \r\n\r\nGame Options\r\n\r\nPractice Mode:  The computer will not bid.  Allowing the player to always win bid and practice different plays.\r\nScoring - Conventional and Progressive:  With Conventional scoring the bid winner may go into negatives if the bid is not acheived.
